Selling Silkworms and Bees: Intra-Hanafi Differences
Explains the disagreement among Hanafi imams on selling silkworms and bees separately

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on selling silkworms and bees and identify the mufta bihi for each.

Core Idea
The Hanafi fatwa allows selling silkworms absolutely and bees if enclosed, despite disagreement among the founding imams.

The sale of living insects like silkworms and bees raises questions about what qualifies as property in Islamic law. This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: while Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (the Sahibayn) differ, the later fatwa adopts the most flexible view—allowing silkworm sales unconditionally and bee sales when the insects are confined. Understanding this dispute reveals how benefit (manfa'ah) and custom ('urf) influence rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two items and the general rule
The passage opens with a ruling: silkworms cannot be sold except with the silk, nor bees except with the beehive. This establishes the baseline before the ikhtilaf.
2
Map the ikhtilaf for silkworms
Abu Hanifa prohibits sale because worms are insects (hawāmm). Abu Yusuf allows if silk has appeared (as a sign of value). Muhammad allows absolutely because they provide benefit. Identify each position.
3
Map the ikhtilaf for bees
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf prohibit selling bees separately. Muhammad allows if they are enclosed (muḥraz), comparable to non-edible but useful animals like mules.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its basis
The text states 'wal-fatwa 'ala qawl Muhammad' – the fatwa relies on Muhammad's view. The underlying reason is that benefit (manfa'ah) makes the item property, and custom permits these sales.
5
Apply to a modern scenario
Consider a farmer selling live silkworms to a silk producer: under the fatwa, the sale is valid. For bees, if the bees are in a transportable box (enclosed), the sale is valid; if they are free-swarming, it is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال: وما حكم بيع دود القز والنحل ؟
الجواب: لا يجوز بيع دود القز إلا مع القز، وكذا بيع النحل إلا مع الكوَّارات.
دود القز: أما الدود فلا يجوز بيعه عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه من الهوام، وعند أبي يوسف يجوز إذا ظهر فيه القز تبعا، وعند محمد يجوز كيفما كان؛ لكونه منتفعا به، والفتوى على قول محمد. وفي "المصباح": القز مُعرَّب قال الليث هو ما يعمل منه الإبريسم، ولهذا قال بعضهم: القز والإبريسم مثل الحنطة والدقيق، " البحر الرائق: (٨٥/٦).
من
بيع
-
لغة
النحل: لا يجوز بيع النحل عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد: يجوز إذا كان مُحَرزًا، وإن كان لا يؤكل كالبغل والحمار، وذكر القدوري أن بيعه للكوَّارة فيها عسل جائز والكوارة بضم الكاف وتشديد الواو، مُعسل النحل إذا سُوِّي من طين، وفي "المصباح" : كوَّارة النحل - بالضم والتخفيف والتثقيل معسلها في الشمع، وقيل: بيتها إذا كان فيه العسل من "البحر الرائق": (٨٤/٦).
Question: What is the ruling on selling silkworms and bees? Answer: It is not permissible to sell silkworms except with the silk, and similarly bees except with the beehives. Silkworms: As for the worms, selling them is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa because they are insects; according to Abu Yusuf, it is permissible if the silk has appeared in them as a follow-up; according to Muhammad, it is permissible in any case because they are benefited from, and the fatwa is on Muhammad's view. In al-Misbah: al-qazz is Arabized; al-Layth said it is what is used to make silk, and for this reason some said: al-qazz and ibrisim (raw silk) are like wheat and flour. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (6/85). Bees: Selling bees is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Muhammad said it is permissible if they are enclosed (muhraz), even if they are not eaten like mules and donkeys. Al-Quduri mentioned that selling the beehive with honey is permissible. The kawwāra is the beehive made from clay. In al-Misbah: kawwārat al-nahl is the beehive in wax; or their home if it contains honey. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (6/84).
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage deals with the permissibility of selling silkworms and bees as separate commodities. The initial answer states that they cannot be sold alone; they must be sold with their product (silk or honey/hive). Then it delves into the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. For silkworms: Abu Hanifa forbids it because worms are considered insects (hawāmm) which are not considered property worthy of independent sale. Abu Yusuf allows it if the silk has already appeared inside them, as then they are considered an attachment to the silk. Muhammad allows it absolutely because they have benefit (they produce silk). The relied-upon fatwa is on Muhammad's view. For bees: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf prohibit selling them separately, but Muhammad allows it if they are enclosed (muḥraz), i.e., in a hive or container. The sale of the beehive (kawwāra) with honey is unanimously permissible. This shows the Hanafi school's flexibility: emphasis on benefit and custom, even at odds with the strictness of the two senior imams.

Key Terms
دود القز (dud al-qazz): Silkworms; the larvae that produce silk.
النحل (al-nahl): Bees; insects that produce honey.
الكوَّارة (al-kawwāra): A beehive made from clay or wax; the place where bees live.
مُحرَز (muhraz): Enclosed, confined; condition for the permissibility of selling bees according to Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is permissible only if sold with the silk.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa permits selling silkworms unconditionally and bees when enclosed, based on Muhammad's view emphasizing benefit and custom.

Effect and Annulment of a Fasid Sale
Ruling on fasid sale with conditions and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a fasid sale, explain the effect of possession, and determine the validity of subsequent acts by the buyer.

Core Idea
A fasid sale transfers ownership upon possession, but must be annulled; the buyer's subsequent sale to a third party is valid.

In Hanafi law, sales are not simply valid or void—there is a third category: fasid (defective). A fasid sale is one that contains a defect in a non-essential condition. This passage explains that such a sale still passes ownership to the buyer when he takes possession with the seller's permission, but both parties must annul the contract. If the buyer does not annul but instead sells the item to someone else in a valid sale, that second sale is enforceable. Understanding this ruling is crucial for distinguishing between different types of invalidity in Islamic commercial law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept of fasid sale
Recognize that in Hanafi fiqh, a fasid sale is one that is defective in a non-essential condition. It is distinct from a batil (void) sale, which transfers no ownership.
2
Understand the effect of possession
When the buyer takes possession of the item with the seller's permission in a fasid sale, he becomes the owner and is liable to pay the fair market price (qīmah).
3
Recognize the obligation to annul
Both parties are obligated (wajib) to annul the contract to remove the defect, as the transaction involves sin (ma'siyah). The obligation persists as long as the item remains with the buyer.
4
Examine the validity of subsequent disposal
If the buyer sells the item to a third party in a valid sale, or gives it away, frees a slave, makes a waqf, etc., the original fasid sale becomes binding and cannot be annulled. The subsequent act is valid.
5
Consider the profit from subsequent disposal
The passage asks about profit but does not fully answer. From Hanafi rules, since the buyer owned the item at the time of resale, any profit is permissible for him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال: وما حكم البيع الفاسد؟
الجواب: إذا تبايعا بيعا فاسدا، وفي العقد ،عوضان كل واحد منهما مال، وقبض المشتري المبيع بأمر البائع ملك المشتري المبيع ولزمته قيمته، لكن يجب على كل واحد منهما فسخ هذا البيع مطاوعة لأمر الشرع.
السؤال: كان عليهما أن يفسخاه، لكن لم يعملا بذلك، وباع المشتري هذا المال، هل نفذ بيعه هذا؟
الجواب: نعم، ينفذ.
السؤال: باع المشتري ما اشتراه شراء فاسدا وحصل له في ذلك ربح، ما حكم هذا الربح ؟
لأمر الشرع: ويجب على كل واحد منهما فسخه قبل القبض أو بعده، ما دام المبيع بحاله في يد المشتري إعداما للفساد؛ لأنه معصية فيجب رفعها، من "الدر المختار".
ينفذ: فإن باع المشتري المُشترى فاسدا من غير بائعه بيعا صحيحا باتا، أو وهبه وسلم أو أعتقه أو كاتبه أو وقفه وقفا صحيحا، وأخرجه عن ملكه أو رهنه أو أوصى به ثم مات نفذ البيع الفاسد في جميع ما مر، وامتنع الفسخ التعلق حق العبد به من "الدر المختار".
Question: What is the ruling on a fasid sale? Answer: If they mutually transact a fasid sale, and in the contract there are two compensations, each being property, and the buyer takes possession of the sold item with the seller's command, the buyer owns the sold item and is liable for its price, but it is obligatory for each of them to cancel this sale in obedience to the command of Sharia. Question: They were supposed to cancel it, but they did not do so, and the buyer sold this property – does his sale become effective? Answer: Yes, it becomes effective. Question: The buyer sold what he purchased in a fasid sale and made a profit in doing so – what is the ruling on this profit? For the command of Sharia: It is obligatory for each of them to cancel it before or after possession, as long as the sold item remains in the buyer's hand, to eradicate the corruption, because it is a sin and must be removed (from al-Durr al-Mukhtar). It becomes effective: For the buyer sold what was purchased in a fasid sale to someone other than his seller in a sound, irrevocable sale, or gifted it, gave it, set it free, made a kitabah, made a valid waqf, removed it from his ownership, pawned it, or bequeathed it and then died – the fasid sale becomes effective in all that was mentioned, and the right of the slave is established and cancellation is prevented (from al-Durr al-Mukhtar).
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage states the general ruling for a fasid (invalid) sale. In Hanafi fiqh, a fasid sale is one that is defective in a non-essential condition. The buyer becomes owner of the item upon taking possession with the seller's permission, and is liable to pay its fair price (qīmah). However, both parties are obligated to rescind the contract because the defect must be removed. If the buyer does not rescind and instead sells the item to a third party in a valid sale, that subsequent sale is valid and enforceable. The question about the profit from such a resale is raised, but the text does not directly answer; however, from the Hanafi rules, the profit is permissible for the buyer because he owned the item at the time of the resale. The marginal notes from al-Durr al-Mukhtar emphasize that the obligation to rescind persists as long as the item is still in the buyer's possession, but if the buyer takes certain actions (giving, freeing, etc.) that remove the item from his ownership, the original fasid sale becomes final and cannot be rescinded. This illustrates the Hanafi approach of balancing legal validity with corrective measures.

Key Terms
البيع الفاسد (al-bay' al-fāsid): A sale that is defective in a non-essential condition; it transfers ownership upon possession but must be annulled.
العوضان (al-'iwaḍān): The two compensations (price and sold item) in a contract.
القيمة (al-qīmah): The fair market price; the buyer becomes liable to pay this in a fasid sale.
الفسخ (al-faskh): Annulment of the contract; obligatory in a fasid sale to remove the defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if the buyer in a fasid sale sells the item to a third party in a valid sale?
A) The second sale is invalid because the first sale is fasid.
B) The second sale is valid and the original fasid sale becomes binding.
C) The second sale is suspended until the first sale is annulled.
D) The second sale is valid only if the buyer first annuls the fasid sale.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a fasid sale transfers ownership to the buyer upon possession, but the contract must be annulled; however, if the buyer subsequently disposes of the property in a valid transaction, the original sale becomes binding and cannot be rescinded.

Selling Silkworms and Bees: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling beneficial insects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on selling silkworms and bees, explain the basis for each, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school differs internally on selling beneficial insects; the fatwa follows Muhammad's view allowing sale.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-madhhab dispute on the permissibility of selling silkworms and bees independently. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold restrictions, while Muhammad permits sale based on benefit. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi methodology handles emerging commodities and the role of istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three imams' positions
List what each of the three major Hanafi imams says about selling silkworms and bees: Abu Hanifa prohibits, Abu Yusuf permits silkworms conditionally, Muhammad permits unconditionally. For bees, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf prohibit, Muhammad permits if contained.
Note the difference between silkworms and bees in conditions.
2
Understand the rationale
For each position, identify the underlying legal reasoning: Abu Hanifa sees silkworms as hawamm (creeping things) not property; Abu Yusuf uses taba'iyyah (subordination) when silk appears; Muhammad uses istihsan based on manfa'ah (benefit). For bees, the containment condition (muhrazan) is key.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) dispute.
3
Recognize the tarjih
The text explicitly states 'والفتوى على قول محمد' (the fatwa is on Muhammad's opinion). This means the operative ruling for practice follows Muhammad's view.
Tarjih within the madhhab is a necessary skill.
4
Apply the principle
Consider how the principle of manfa'ah (benefit) can override the default prohibition on selling non-property objects. This demonstrates Hanafi istihsan as a method of legal reasoning.
This shows the flexibility of the Hanafi school in commercial matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال: وما حكم بيع دود القز والنحل ؟
الجواب: لا يجوز بيع دود القز إلا مع القز، وكذا بيع النحل إلا مع الكوَّارات.
دود القز: أما الدود فلا يجوز بيعه عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه من الهوام، وعند أبي يوسف يجوز إذا ظهر فيه القز تبعا، وعند محمد يجوز كيفما كان؛ لكونه منتفعا به، والفتوى على قول محمد. وفي "المصباح": القز مُعرَّب قال الليث هو ما يعمل منه الإبريسم، ولهذا قال بعضهم: القز والإبريسم مثل الحنطة والدقيق. البحر الرائق: (٨٥/٦).
النحل: لا يجوز بيع النحل عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد: يجوز إذا كان مُحَرزًا، وإن كان لا يؤكل كالبغل والحمار، وذكر القدوري أن بيعه للكوَّارة فيها عسل جائز والكوارة بضم الكاف وتشديد الواو، مُعسل النحل إذا سُوِّي من طين، وفي "المصباح": كوَّارة النحل - بالضم والتخفيف والتثقيل معسلها في الشمع، وقيل: بيتها إذا كان فيه العسل من البحر الرائق: (٨٤/٦).
Question: What is the ruling on selling silkworms and bees? Answer: It is not permissible to sell silkworms except with the silk, and likewise selling bees except with the beehives. Silkworms: As for the worm, it is not permissible to sell it according to Abu Hanifa because it is among creeping things. According to Abu Yusuf, it is permissible if silk has appeared in it as a subordinate. According to Muhammad, it is permissible regardless because benefit is derived from it, and the fatwa is on Muhammad's opinion. In al-Misbah: al-qazz is arabicized; al-Layth said it is what silk is made from, hence some said al-qazz and al-ibrisam are like wheat and flour. al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (6/85). Bees: Selling bees is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said it is permissible if they are contained, even if not eaten like the mule and donkey. Al-Quduri mentioned that selling them with the beehive containing honey is permissible. Al-Kuwwara (beehive) with a damm on the kaf and tashdid on the waw, the honeycomb of bees when made of clay. In al-Misbah: kuwwarat al-nahl – with damm and lightening and heavyening – its honeycomb in wax, or it is said its house when it has honey. From al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (6/84).
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of selling silkworms and bees independently. The text opens with a general ruling: silkworms may only be sold together with silk, and bees only with their hives. The commentary then details the positions of the three major Hanafi imams. For silkworms, Abu Hanifa prohibits selling the worm alone because it is considered a creeping insect (hawamm) and thus not legally property. Abu Yusuf allows it if silk has already appeared, as the worm then becomes subordinate to the silk (taba'iyyah). Muhammad allows it unconditionally because the worm is beneficial (yuntafa' bihi) for silk production, and the fatwa is on Muhammad's view. For bees, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf prohibit independent sale, while Muhammad allows it if the bees are confined (muhrazan) in a hive, analogizing them to non-edible animals like mules and donkeys that can be sold. The text also references Al-Quduri's position that selling bees with a hive containing honey is permissible. The passage emphasizes the reliance on benefit (manfa'ah) as the basis for permissibility in Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
دود القز (dud al-qazz): Silkworms, the larvae of the silkmoth that produce silk fibers.
الكوَّارات (al-kuwwarat): Beehives, specifically those made of clay or wax containing honey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Not permissible according to all Hanafi imams.
B) Permissible according to Muhammad and the fatwa.
C) Permissible only if silk has appeared, according to Abu Yusuf.
D) Permissible only if the worms are confined.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa permits the independent sale of silkworms and bees, following Muhammad's view based on benefit (manfa'ah).

Ruling on an Invalid Sale (Bay' Fasid)
Defines a fasid sale and its consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a fasid sale, explain the effect of possession on ownership, and identify when rescission becomes impossible.

Core Idea
A fasid sale transfers ownership upon possession but must be rescinded; subsequent valid dispositions make it permanent.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on an invalid (fasid) sale. Unlike a batil sale, a fasid sale is not automatically void; it has legal effect until rescinded. The key distinction is that possession with the seller's consent vests ownership in the buyer, creating a religious obligation to rescind. However, if the buyer makes a valid disposition of the property (e.g., selling to a third party), the original fasid sale becomes binding and rescission is no longer possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? A fasid sale (invalid sale). Determine its hukm: it is a sin (haram) but not void ab initio; rescission is wajib.
The text states it is a sin (ma'siyah) that must be removed.
2
Locate the condition for ownership transfer
Find the condition under which the buyer becomes owner: possession (qabd) with the seller's command (bi-amr al-ba'i). Note that both compensations must be mal (wealth).
The text: 'In the contract there are two compensations each being wealth, and the buyer takes possession of the sold item by the seller's command.'
3
Understand the obligation to rescind
Why is rescission wajib? Because the contract involves sin (ifsad). The proof is the general command of Shari'ah to avoid corruption. Rescission is obligatory before or after possession as long as the item is still with the buyer.
The text: 'It is obligatory for each of them to rescind it... because it is a sin, so it must be removed.'
4
Analyze the effect of subsequent dispositions
What happens if the buyer makes a valid disposition (sale, gift, manumission, etc.) before rescinding? The second transaction is valid, and the original fasid sale becomes effective; rescission is no longer possible.
The text lists several examples: 'If the buyer sells... or gives as a gift... the invalid sale takes effect.'
5
Derive the practical consequence
The ruling balances religious duty with property rights. Once a third party acquires rights, the original fasid sale is enforced to protect those rights.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) compared to other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال: وما حكم البيع الفاسد؟
الجواب: إذا تبايعا بيعا فاسدا، وفي العقد عوضان كل واحد منهما مال، وقبض المشتري المبيع بأمر البائع ملك المشتري المبيع ولزمته قيمته، لكن يجب على كل واحد منهما فسخ هذا البيع مطاوعة لأمر الشرع.
السؤال: كان عليهما أن يفسخاه، لكن لم يعملا بذلك، وباع المشتري هذا المال، هل نفذ بيعه هذا؟
الجواب: نعم، ينفذ.
لأمر الشرع: ويجب على كل واحد منهما فسخه قبل القبض أو بعده، ما دام المبيع بحاله في يد المشتري إعداما للفساد؛ لأنه معصية فيجب رفعها، من "الدر المختار".
ينفذ: فإن باع المشتري المُشترى فاسدا من غير بائعه بيعا صحيحا باتا، أو وهبه وسلم أو أعتقه أو كاتبه أو وقفه وقفا صحيحا، وأخرجه عن ملكه أو رهنه أو أوصى به ثم مات نفذ البيع الفاسد في جميع ما مر، وامتنع الفسخ التعلق حق العبد به من "الدر المختار".
Question: What is the ruling on an invalid sale? Answer: If two people transact an invalid sale, and in the contract there are two compensations each being wealth, and the buyer takes possession of the sold item by the seller's command, the buyer owns the sold item and its price becomes obligatory upon him, but each of them must rescind this sale in obedience to the command of the Shari'ah. Question: It was incumbent upon them to rescind it, but they did not do so, and the buyer sold that property, is his sale valid? Answer: Yes, it is valid. For the command of the Shari'ah: It is obligatory for each of them to rescind it before or after possession, as long as the sold item remains in the buyer's hand, to nullify the corruption; because it is a sin, so it must be removed. From al-Durr al-Mukhtar. It is valid: If the buyer sells what he bought invalidly to someone other than his seller in a sound and final sale, or gives it as a gift, or sets free, or writes a kitaba, or gives it as a valid waqf, or removes it from his ownership, or pawns it, or bequeaths it then dies, the invalid sale takes effect in all that has passed, and rescission is prevented due to the right of the slave attaching to it. From al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on an invalid (fasid) sale. The key conditions: both parties exchange property that qualifies as mal (wealth), and the buyer takes possession with the seller's consent. In such a case, the buyer becomes owner of the item and is liable for its price (qimah). However, there is a religious obligation (wajib) on both parties to rescind the contract to eliminate the sin of engaging in a corrupt transaction. The proof is the general command of Shari'ah to avoid corruption (ifsad). If the buyer subsequently sells the item to a third party, that second sale is valid and takes precedence; the original invalid sale is then deemed effective, and rescission is no longer possible because the item has transferred to a new owner. The commentary from al-Durr al-Mukhtar elaborates that various dispositions like gift, manumission, waiver, or waqf also prevent rescission. The ruling balances between upholding property rights (milk) and religious obligation to rectify the contract.

Key Terms
البيع الفاسد (al-bay' al-fasid): An invalid sale that is defective in some condition but not fundamentally void (batil); it transfers ownership upon possession but must be rescinded.
مطاوعة لأمر الشرع (mutawa'atan li-amr al-shar'): In obedience to the command of the Shari'ah, i.e., the religious duty to avoid sin by rescinding the fasid contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer acquires an item through a fasid sale and then sells it to a third party before rescinding, what is the ruling?
A) The second sale is invalid because the first sale was fasid.
B) The second sale is valid and the original fasid sale cannot be rescinded.
C) The buyer must return the item to the original seller first.
D) The buyer must give the profit to charity.

Key Takeaway
A fasid sale in Hanafi law transfers ownership upon possession with the seller's command, but both parties must rescind it; however, if the buyer makes a valid disposition, the rescission is waived and the sale becomes binding.

Profit from a Fasid Sale: Buyer Must Give Charity
Ruling on profit from an invalid sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on profit from a fasid sale and distinguish between the buyer's obligation to give charity and the seller's entitlement to keep his profit.

Core Idea
Profit from an invalid sale is tainted; the buyer must give it in charity, but the seller keeps his profit.

This lesson addresses a common question in Islamic finance: what happens to profit earned by a buyer who resells an item he purchased through an invalid (fasid) sale? The Hanafi school provides a clear distinction: the buyer's profit is not lawful and must be given in charity, while the seller's profit on the price remains lawful. Understanding this ruling helps maintain purity of earnings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and parties
Recognize the scenario: a buyer purchases an item via a fasid sale, then resells it and makes a profit. The question is about the ruling on that profit for the buyer.
2
State the ruling for the buyer
The text clearly states: 'This profit is not lawful for him and he must give it in charity.' The buyer cannot keep the profit; he must dispose of it as sadaqah.
The phrase 'la yatibu' indicates the profit is morally and legally impure.
3
Contrast with the seller's position
The commentary explains that the seller, despite the sale being fasid, may keep the profit he earned on the price. He is not required to give charity.
The seller's sale is not batil; only the buyer's acquisition is defective due to the invalid purchase.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The defect in the buyer's ownership means any profit from that ownership is tainted. The seller's profit on the price is separate because his sale, though fasid, is not void (batil) and the price is considered compensation for the item.
This principle is rooted in the Hanafi concept that a fasid contract transfers ownership with a defect, and profits from such ownership must be purified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال: باع المشتري ما اشتراه شراء فاسدا وحصل له في ذلك ربح، ما حكم هذا الربح ؟
الجواب: هذا الربح لا يطيب له وعليه أن يتصدق به.
أن يتصدق به طاب للبائع ما ربحه في ثمن البيع الفاسد، ولا يطيب للمشتري ربح المبيع، فلا يتصدق الأول أي البائع، ويتصدق المشتري، من "البحر الرائق".
Question: The buyer sold what he bought in an invalid sale and obtained profit thereby, what is the ruling on this profit? Answer: This profit is not lawful for him and he must give it in charity. To give it in charity: It is lawful for the seller what he profited in the price of the invalid sale, and it is not lawful for the buyer the profit of the sold item. So the first (i.e., the seller) does not give charity, and the buyer gives charity. From al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This is a concise ruling: when a buyer makes a profit from reselling an item acquired through an invalid (fasid) purchase, that profit is not halal for him and must be given as sadaqah (charity). The commentary clarifies that the seller, on the other hand, may keep any profit he made on the price received, because his original sale was only fasid, not batil. The profit earned by the buyer is considered unlawful because the basis of his ownership is defective. The ruling rests on the principle that gains from invalid contracts are tainted and must be purified by charity. This is a mufta bihi position from authoritative texts like al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Key Terms
لا يطيب (la yatibu): Not lawful/pure; the profit is considered tainted (ghayr tayyib) and must be disposed of by charity.
بيع فاسد (bay' fasid): An invalid sale; a contract that is defective in its conditions or pillars (e.g., missing a condition of validity) but not completely void (batil). Ownership transfers but is defective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must the buyer do with the profit from a fasid sale?
A) Keep it, because he owned the item.
B) Give it in charity.
C) Return it to the seller.
D) Spend it on himself.

Key Takeaway
Profit from a fasid sale is tainted for the buyer, who must give it in charity; the seller's profit on the price is lawful and may be kept.

Auction Sale (Bay' Man Yazid) and Its Proof
Ruling on auction sale with hadith proof and whether seller is bound by final bid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on auction sales and explain why the seller is not bound to accept the highest bid, citing the prophetic proof.

Core Idea
Auction sales are permissible (mubah), but the seller retains full discretion to accept or reject the final bid.

This lesson addresses two key questions about auction sales (bay' man yazid): their permissibility and the seller's obligation. The Hanafi school rules that auction selling is permissible based on the Prophet's own practice. However, the seller is not compelled to sell to the highest bidder; he may choose to accept or decline. This ruling is supported by a hadith narrated by Abu Dawud, which we will examine.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
State the Hanafi position: auction sale is mubah (permissible), and the seller is not obligated to accept the highest bid.
These two rulings are the core of the lesson.
2
Locate the proof
Find the hadith cited: the Prophet sold a cup and a rug for the Ansari man by calling for bids.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the Prophet's action indicates permissibility: his fi'l (act) shows jawaz unless proven otherwise.
Hanafi usul: fi'l al-nabi indicates permissibility, not obligation.
4
Understand seller's choice
The text explicitly says the seller is 'mukhtar' (has choice) and 'la jabra alayhi' (no compulsion).
The seller may accept or reject any bid.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon fatwa: auction is permissible and the seller is not bound.
This is the established Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال: و ما حكم بيع من يزيد؟
الجواب: لا بأس ببيع من يزيد؛ لما أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم باع قدحا وحلسا كذلك.
السؤال: وهل يلزم البائع - في بيع من يزيد - أن يبيع المال بالثمن الأخير؟
الجواب: لا يلزمه ذلك بل هو مختار في ذلك، لا جبر عليه.
باع قدحا وحلسا: روى أبو داود (باب) ما تجوز فيه المسألة عن أنس أن رجلا من الأنصار أتى النبي يسأله، فقال : أما في بيتك شيء؟ قال بلی حلس نلبس بعضه ونبسط بعضه، وقعب (وهو القدح) نشرب فيه الماء، قال: ائتني بهما، فأتاه بهما، فأخذهما رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بيده وقال: من يشتري هذين. قال رجل : أنا من قال: من يزيد على درهم؟ مرتين أو ثلاثا، قال رجل: أنا آخذهما بدرهمين، فأعطاهما إياه وأخذ الدرهمين فأعطاهما الأنصاري (إلى آخر الحديث).
Question: What is the ruling on sale by increase (auction)? Answer: There is no harm in sale by increase because the Prophet (peace be upon him) sold a cup and a rug in that manner. Question: Is the seller obliged in an auction sale to sell the item for the last price? Answer: He is not obliged; rather he has a choice in that, no compulsion upon him. He sold a cup and a rug: Abu Dawud narrated (chapter: what is allowed in asking) from Anas that a man from the Ansar came to the Prophet asking him. He said: 'Is there anything in your house?' He said: 'Yes, a rug we wear part and spread part, and a cup from which we drink water.' He said: 'Bring them to me.' So he brought them. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) took them in his hand and said: 'Who will buy these two items?' A man said: 'I will take them for a dirham.' He said: 'Will anyone increase more than a dirham?' two or three times. A man said: 'I will take them for two dirhams.' So he gave them to him and took the two dirhams and gave them to the Ansari (to the end of the hadith).
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues related to auction sales (bay' man yazid). First, the permissibility: the answer confirms it is permissible (la ba'sa) based on the explicit action of the Prophet (peace be upon him), who himself conducted an auction for a cup and a rug belonging to an Ansari companion. The hadith, narrated by Abu Dawud, provides the direct proof (dalil naqli). Second, the seller's obligation: the seller is not forced to accept the highest bid; he has full choice (mukhtar) and is not compelled (la jabra 'alayhi). This means the auction process is a form of negotiation, not a binding offer. The hadith is quoted in full to establish the sunnah. The ruling is clear: auction is valid and the seller retains discretion.

Key Terms
بيع من يزيد (bay' man yazid): Sale by increase, i.e., an auction where buyers bid increasing prices and the seller accepts the highest offer.
حلس (hils): A rug or mat made of hair or wool, spread for sitting and used as bedding.

Key Takeaway
Auction sales are permissible (mubah) in Hanafi fiqh, and the seller retains full discretion to accept or reject the final bid, based on the prophetic sunnah.

Rulings of Dhimmis in Sales
Rules for non-Muslim subjects regarding validity of sales contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of sales contracts involving wine and pork for dhimmis and distinguish it from the ruling for Muslims.

Core Idea
Dhimmis' sales are Islamic-law governed except for wine and pork, which are valid for them as per their faith.

This lesson addresses a key exception in Hanafi commercial law: while dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects) are generally bound by Islamic rules of sales, contracts involving wine and pork are considered valid for them because these items are permissible in their religions. This reflects the Hanafi principle that dhimmis are not required to observe Islamic prohibitions on what is lawful for them. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying contract law in a pluralistic society.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the general rule
Recognize that the ruling distinguishes between Muslims and dhimmis. The general principle is that dhimmis are like Muslims in sales: their contracts are judged by Islamic standards of validity (sihhah) and invalidity (fasad).
This includes rules on gharar, riba, etc.
2
Identify the exception
Note the exception: wine (khamr) and pork (khinzir) are excluded from the general rule. For dhimmis, contracts involving these items are considered valid, unlike for Muslims.
The exception is specific to these two items.
3
Understand the analogy
The text draws an analogy: a dhimmi's contract on wine is like a Muslim's contract on grape juice (valid), and a dhimmi's contract on pork is like a Muslim's contract on a sheep (valid). This highlights that these items are halal for dhimmis in their religion.
The analogy reinforces that validity is based on permissibility for the contracting party.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a scenario, such as a dhimmi selling wine in his shop, determine the validity: the contract is sahih (valid) for the dhimmi, whereas a Muslim selling wine would be batil (void).
The ruling does not change if the buyer is Muslim; the focus is on the seller's capacity.
5
State the consequence
Summarize: For dhimmis, wine and pork sales are valid and enforceable; ownership transfers and consideration is lawful. For Muslims, such contracts are void and have no legal effect.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال: أهل الذمة الذين يسكنون في دار الإسلام هل يلزمهم رعاية أحكام الإسلام في البيوع، من حيث الصحة والفساد؟
الجواب: هم في ذلك كالمسلمين إلا في الخمر والخنزير خاصة، فإن عقدهم على الخمر كعقد المسلم على العصير وعقدهم على الخنزير كعقد المسلم على الشاة.
Question: Non-Muslim subjects (ahl al-dhimmah) living in the abode of Islam – are they obligated to observe the rulings of Islam in sales, in terms of validity and invalidity? Answer: They are in that like Muslims except regarding wine and pork specifically, for their contract on wine is like a Muslim's contract on grape juice, and their contract on pork is like a Muslim's contract on a sheep.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage clarifies the legal capacity of dhimmis (protected non-Muslims) in commercial transactions within Islamic territory. The general principle is that dhimmis are subject to the same laws of sale as Muslims: contracts are judged by Islamic rules of validity (sihhah) and invalidity (fasad). However, an exception is made for wine (khamr) and pork (khinzir). For a Muslim, selling these items is invalid because they are najis and forbidden. For a dhimmi, the contract is considered valid (like a Muslim's contract on grape juice or a sheep) because these items are permissible in their faith. The analogy drawn is clear: the dhimmi's wine contract corresponds to a Muslim's contract on grape juice (which is halal), and pork corresponds to sheep (halal meat). This reflects the Hanafi view that dhimmis are not bound by Islamic prohibitions regarding their own religiously lawful items, as long as the transaction does not involve open sin in Islamic public order.

Key Terms
أهل الذمة (ahl al-dhimmah): Non-Muslim subjects living under Muslim rule who pay jizyah and are protected, allowed to practice their religion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For dhimmis, wine and pork contracts are valid and treated like permissible items for Muslims; this is a key exception in Hanafi sale law.

Prohibition of Sale During Jumu'ah Call
Introduces disliked sales with Quranic proof prohibiting sale at Jumu'ah call.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of sale during the Jumu'ah call as haram and identify the Quranic verse as its primary proof.

Core Idea
Trade during the Jumu'ah call is prohibited by the clear command of the Qur'an — leave trade and proceed to prayer.

This lesson introduces the category of disliked sales (al-buyu' al-makruhah) through a direct Quranic command. The verse from Surah al-Jumu'ah establishes a clear prohibition against engaging in trade at the time of the Friday prayer call. Understanding this ruling requires recognizing the authoritative proof (dalil naqli) and its implications in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Read the verse and determine what act is being prohibited. The act is selling (al-bay') during the call to Jumu'ah prayer. The ruling from the imperative 'dharu al-bay'a' is prohibition (haram).
In Hanafi usul, a command to leave (nahy) indicates haram unless there is a countervailing evidence.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the Quranic verse itself: Surah al-Jumu'ah (62):9. It is a primary textual proof (dalil naqli) with qati' thubut (certain transmission) and qati' dalalah (clear meaning).
The verse is from the Mushaf, so its authenticity is unquestionable.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The legal implication comes from the imperative verb 'dharu' (leave/abandon). In Hanafi usul, a direct order to abandon an act signifies prohibition (haram). This makes trading during that time sinful.
The section heading 'disliked sales' includes this strong prohibition; it is makruh tahrimi, not merely tanzihi.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
All schools agree on the prohibition of engaging in trade during the Jumu'ah call. However, they differ on the validity of a sale contract concluded at that time. The Hanafi position is that the contract is valid (sahih) but the act is haram.
The passage does not discuss contract validity; it only establishes the prohibition. This step is for context.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The mufta bihi is the prohibition based on the clear Quranic text. No tarjih is needed as the evidence is primary. The ruling is established from Zahir al-Riwayah and is firm.
The authority weight is highest (Quran).

البيوع المكروهة

Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of a section on disliked sales (al-buyu' al-makruhah). It opens with a direct Quranic verse (Surah al-Jumu'ah: 9) which commands believers to leave trade when the call to Friday prayer is made. This verse serves as the primary proof (dalil naqli) that selling at that time is prohibited (haram during the call) and thus considered a disliked sale in a broader sense. Although the term 'disliked' (makruh) can imply less than haram, the verse uses the imperative 'leave' (dharu), which indicates a prohibition. In Hanafi usul, such a prohibition from the Quran renders the act haram, but the section heading 'disliked sales' suggests that the focus is on sales that are discouraged due to conflicting with religious obligations. This is an introductory piece; further rulings on disliked sales are expected to follow.

Key Terms
البيوع المكروهة (al-buyu' al-makruhah): Disliked sales; a category of sales that are discouraged due to violating a recommended or obligatory practice.

The Prohibited and Disliked Sales in Hanafi Fiqh
Lists and explains four prohibited sales with their proofs and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four types of prohibited sales (najsh, bidding over a bid, intercepting caravans, urbanite selling for Bedouin), state their Hanafi ruling (makruh tahrimi), and explain the conditions under which they become permissible.

Core Idea
A prohibited sale is still valid; sin lies in the action, not the contract.

This passage from Al-Tashil al-Daruri discusses sales that are prohibited (makruh tahrimi) according to the Hanafi school. The author lists four types: najsh, bidding over another's bid, intercepting caravans, and an urbanite selling for a Bedouin. The commentary clarifies that the prohibition does not invalidate the contract; the sale remains valid but sinful. Understanding these rulings is essential for avoiding forbidden transactions in everyday trade.

Guided Path
1
Identify each prohibited sale
List the four sales: najsh, sawm 'ala sawm, talqi al-jalb, bay' al-hadir lil-badi. Understand the basic definition of each.
The passage begins by mentioning these four after the Friday sale prohibition.
2
Understand the Hanafi legal category
Recognize that these are classified as makruh tahrimi: the contract is valid (sahih) but the action is sinful. The commentator emphasizes that 'makruh' here refers to the effect on contract validity, not the severity of prohibition.
The distinction between makruh and fasid is crucial.
3
Examine the dalil for each
For each sale, note the hadith proof provided (najsh: 'la tanajashu'; sawm: hadith against bidding over brother's bid; talqi: hadith from Ibn Abbas; bay' al-hadir: same hadith). Understand how the evidence supports the prohibition.
The proofs are from Sahihayn and other sources.
4
Apply the conditions for permissibility
For each sale, identify when it becomes permissible: najsh is allowed if the commodity hasn't reached its value; sawm is allowed if no agreement is reached; talqi is allowed if no harm or deception; bay' al-hadir is allowed if there is no scarcity/harm.
The Hanafi approach often restricts the general prohibition to cases of harm or exploitation.

فالبيع عند أذان الجمعة وبعده ممنوع حتى يفرغ من صلاة الجمعة. ونهى عن النجش ، وعن السوم على سوم غيره، وعن تلقي الجلب، وعن بيع الحاضر للبادي. فائدة من ملك مملوكين صغيرين، أحدهما ذو رحم محرم من الآخر، لا أخره، وليس المراد بكونه دونه في حكم المنع الشرعي، بل في عدم فساد العقد، وإلا فهذه كلها تحريمية لا نعلم خلافا في الإثم، كذا في "فتح القدير"، وقد تقرر في الأصل أن كل منهي قبيح والنجش بفتحتين ويروى إذا تراضي المتعاقدان على مبلغ ثمن في المساومة وإذا لم يركن أحدهما إلى الآخر فلا بأس به. وقوله: عن تلقي الجلب؛ لحديث "الصحيحين" عن ابن عباس  أن رسول الله  أن تتلقى الركبان وأن يبيع حاضر لباد. وللتلقي صورتان إحداهما : أن يتلقاهم المشترون للطعام في سنة حاجة؛ ليبيعوه من أهل البلد بزيادة، وثانيتهما: أن يشتري منهم البلد، لا يعلمون بالسعر. ومحمل النهي عندنا إذا كان يضر بأهل البلد أو لبس أما إذا انتفيا فلا بأس به، وفي من سعر وهم بأرخص "المغرب": جلب الشيء جاء به من بلد إلى بلد للتجارة جلبا، وقوله: "وعن بيع الحاضر" للبادي": لما تقدم من النهي، وهو مقيد كما في "الهداية" بما إذا كان أهل البلد في قحط وعوز، وهو يبيع من أهل البدو طمعا في الثمن الغالي، لما فيه من الإضرار بهم . وفسره في "الاختيار" بأن يجلب البادي السلعة، فيأخذها الحاضر له ليبيعها في وقت بأغلى من السعر الموجود وقت الجلب، فعلى الأول الحاضر مالك بائع والبادي ،مشتر، وعلى الثاني الحاضر مشتر والبادي صاحب السلعة، ويشهد للثاني آخر الحديث: دعوا الناس يرزق الله بعضهم من بعض، ولذا قال في "المجتبى": هذا التفسير أصح، ذكره في "زاد الفقهاء" لموافقة الحديث ملخصا من "البحر الرائق: (١٠٧/٦) قال في "الدر المختار": النجش
وإن كانا كبيرين، فلا بأس بالتفريق بينهما.
The sale at the adhan of Jumu'ah and after it is prohibited until the completion of the Jumu'ah prayer. And he prohibited najsh, and bidding over the bid of another, and intercepting caravans, and the sale of the urbanite for the Bedouin. Benefit: Whoever owns two minor slaves, one of whom is a mahram relative of the other, it is not permissible to separate them by sale, such that he sells this one to a man and that one to another man. Similarly, if one is adult and the other minor, if he separates them, it is disliked but the sale is valid. He said: The sale begins the disliked sales. And since the disliked is below the invalid, he delayed it. But the meaning is not that it is below in terms of legal prohibition, rather in terms of the contract not being void; otherwise, all of these are prohibited and we know no disagreement concerning sinfulness. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And it is established in principle that everything prohibited is evil. Al-najsh (with two fathas and also related with sukun) is that you bid on a commodity with a higher price without intending to buy it, so that another sees you and falls into it. Its origin is from 'bahsh' of game, meaning stirring it up. The hadith of prohibition: 'Do not engage in najsh' in the Sahihayn. Our companions restricted it, as in al-Jawhara, to when the commodity has reached its value. If it has not reached, then there is no prohibition, because it is benefit for a Muslim without harming anyone. And His saying: 'And from bidding over the bid of another' due to the hadith: 'A man should not bid over the bid of his brother, nor propose over his proposal.' And because it contains causing annoyance and harm. This applies when the two parties have agreed on a sum of price in negotiation. If one of them has not inclined to the other, then there is no harm. And His saying: 'From intercepting caravans' due to the hadith of al-Sahihayn from Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah prohibited intercepting riders and that an urbanite should sell for a Bedouin. Interception has two forms: one is that buyers intercept them for food in a year of need to sell it to the people of the town at a higher price; the second is that they buy from them while the people of the town do not know the price. The application of the prohibition for us is when it harms the people of the town or deceives. If both are absent, then there is no harm. In al-Mughrib: 'Jalb' of a thing is bringing it from one town to another for trade. And His saying: 'And from the sale of the urbanite for the Bedouin' due to the preceding prohibition. It is restricted as in al-Hidayah to when the people of the town are in drought and need, and he sells to the Bedouins out of greed for the high price, due to the harm to them. And he interpreted it in al-Ikhtiyar as that the Bedouin brings the goods, and the urbanite takes them to sell at a time at a price higher than the existing price at the time of bringing. According to the first, the urbanite is the owner-seller and the Bedouin is the buyer; according to the second, the urbanite is the buyer and the Bedouin is the owner of the goods. The latter is supported by the end of the hadith: 'Leave the people; Allah provides for some by means of others.' Therefore, it is said in al-Mujtaba: This interpretation is more correct, mentioned in Zad al-Fuqaha' due to agreement with the hadith, summarized from al-Bahr al-Raiq (6/107). Said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: Al-najsh with two fathas or sukun is that you increase in price without intending to buy, or you praise it with what it does not possess to promote it (4/132 on margin of al-Shami). And if both are adults, there is no harm in separating them.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from al-Tashil al-Daruri deals with disliked sales (al-buyu' al-makruhah) and includes an important subsidiary ruling on separating minor slaves who are mahram relatives. The commentator begins by stating that selling during the Friday adhan and afterwards is prohibited (mamn') until the prayer is finished. This is a prohibition related to time, not the contract itself; the contract is valid but sinful. He then lists five prohibited practices: najsh (artificially inflating price by pretending to buy), bidding over another's bid (al-sawm 'ala sawm ghayrihi), intercepting caravans (talqi al-jalb), and an urbanite selling for a Bedouin (bay' al-hadir lil-badi). The commentary explains each: najsh is defined as offering a higher price without intending to buy, to lure another. The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim. Hanafi scholars restrict it to when the commodity has reached its value; if not, it is allowed because it helps the seller without harm. Bidding over another's bid is prohibited based on the hadith and because it causes annoyance. This applies when parties have reached agreement; if no agreement, it's allowed. Intercepting caravans has two forms: buying to resell high in a needy year, or buying while townspeople are unaware. The prohibition applies if it harms or deceives; otherwise, it's allowed. The urbanite selling for the Bedouin is prohibited when the town has scarcity, as it harms. Two interpretations are given: the urbanite sells for the Bedouin, or the urbanite buys from the Bedouin to resell high. The second is preferred. Finally, a 'fa'idah' (benefit) is inserted: If someone owns two minor slaves who are mahram relatives (such as siblings), it is not permissible (la yajuz) to separate them by sale. If one is adult and the other minor, separation is disliked (makruh) but the sale is valid. If both are adults, no problem. The proof for this is given later in the text (on page 206 in the OCR, after iqalah, but belongs here).

Key Terms
النجش (al-najsh): Artificially inflating the price of a commodity by bidding without intending to purchase, to lure another buyer.
السوم على سوم غيره (al-sawm 'ala sawm ghayrihi): Bidding over the bid of another after the parties have agreed on a price.
تلقي الجلب (talqi al-jalb): Intercepting traders bringing goods to town to buy before they reach the market, often to resell at higher prices.
بيع الحاضر للبادي (bay' al-hadir lil-badi): An urbanite selling goods on behalf of a Bedouin (or buying from him to resell), exploiting the Bedouin's ignorance of prices.
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahm muharram): A relative within the prohibited degrees of marriage, i.e., mahram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on najsh (artificially inflating price) when the commodity has not reached its value?
A) It is strictly prohibited and the sale is invalid.
B) It is permissible because it benefits the seller without harming anyone.
C) It is makruh tahrimi and the sale is valid but sinful.
D) It is mandatory to avoid.

Key Takeaway
Prohibited sales are valid but sinful in Hanafi fiqh; their permissibility often depends on the absence of harm or exploitation.

Ruling on Separating Minor Slaves Who Are Mahram
Provides a subsidiary ruling on separating minor mahram slaves in sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on separating minor slaves who are mahram relatives and differentiate between cases where both are minors, one is adult, and both are adults.

Core Idea
Separating minor mahram relatives by sale is prohibited; if one is adult, it is disliked but valid.

The passage includes a 'benefit' (fa'idah) that addresses a specific scenario in the law of sale: when someone owns two minor slaves who are mahram relatives (e.g., siblings), it is not permissible to separate them by selling each to different buyers. If one is an adult and the other a minor, separation is disliked but the sale is valid. If both are adults, there is no restriction. This ruling reflects the Hanafi concern for preserving family bonds among minors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the three cases: both slaves are minor and mahram; one is adult and the other minor and mahram; both are adult and mahram.
The relationship must be mahram (unmarriageable kinship).
2
Determine the hukm for each scenario
For minor-minor: it is not permissible (la yajuz) to separate them. For minor-adult: separation is disliked (makruh) but the sale is valid. For adult-adult: no harm (la ba's) in separating.
Note the progression: prohibition → dislike → permissibility.
3
Understand the basis
The ruling aims to preserve familial care and avoid harm to minors. When both are minors, separation harms them; when one is adult, the adult can care for the minor, so the separation is less severe; when both are adults, no such care is needed.
This is a principle of protecting the vulnerable.

The sale at the adhan of Jumu'ah and after it is prohibited until the completion of the Jumu'ah prayer. And he prohibited najsh, and bidding over the bid of another, and intercepting caravans, and the sale of the urbanite for the Bedouin. Benefit: Whoever owns two minor slaves, one of whom is a mahram relative of the other, it is not permissible to separate them by sale, such that he sells this one to a man and that one to another man. Similarly, if one is adult and the other minor, if he separates them, it is disliked but the sale is valid. He said: The sale begins the disliked sales. And since the disliked is below the invalid, he delayed it. But the meaning is not that it is below in terms of legal prohibition, rather in terms of the contract not being void; otherwise, all of these are prohibited and we know no disagreement concerning sinfulness. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And it is established in principle that everything prohibited is evil. Al-najsh (with two fathas and also related with sukun) is that you bid on a commodity with a higher price without intending to buy it, so that another sees you and falls into it. Its origin is from 'bahsh' of game, meaning stirring it up. The hadith of prohibition: 'Do not engage in najsh' in the Sahihayn. Our companions restricted it, as in al-Jawhara, to when the commodity has reached its value. If it has not reached, then there is no prohibition, because it is benefit for a Muslim without harming anyone. And His saying: 'And from bidding over the bid of another' due to the hadith: 'A man should not bid over the bid of his brother, nor propose over his proposal.' And because it contains causing annoyance and harm. This applies when the two parties have agreed on a sum of price in negotiation. If one of them has not inclined to the other, then there is no harm. And His saying: 'From intercepting caravans' due to the hadith of al-Sahihayn from Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah prohibited intercepting riders and that an urbanite should sell for a Bedouin. Interception has two forms: one is that buyers intercept them for food in a year of need to sell it to the people of the town at a higher price; the second is that they buy from them while the people of the town do not know the price. The application of the prohibition for us is when it harms the people of the town or deceives. If both are absent, then there is no harm. In al-Mughrib: 'Jalb' of a thing is bringing it from one town to another for trade. And His saying: 'And from the sale of the urbanite for the Bedouin' due to the preceding prohibition. It is restricted as in al-Hidayah to when the people of the town are in drought and need, and he sells to the Bedouins out of greed for the high price, due to the harm to them. And he interpreted it in al-Ikhtiyar as that the Bedouin brings the goods, and the urbanite takes them to sell at a time at a price higher than the existing price at the time of bringing. According to the first, the urbanite is the owner-seller and the Bedouin is the buyer; according to the second, the urbanite is the buyer and the Bedouin is the owner of the goods. The latter is supported by the end of the hadith: 'Leave the people; Allah provides for some by means of others.' Therefore, it is said in al-Mujtaba: This interpretation is more correct, mentioned in Zad al-Fuqaha' due to agreement with the hadith, summarized from al-Bahr al-Raiq (6/107). Said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: Al-najsh with two fathas or sukun is that you increase in price without intending to buy, or you praise it with what it does not possess to promote it (4/132 on margin of al-Shami). And if both are adults, there is no harm in separating them.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from al-Tashil al-Daruri deals with disliked sales (al-buyu' al-makruhah) and includes an important subsidiary ruling on separating minor slaves who are mahram relatives. The commentator begins by stating that selling during the Friday adhan and afterwards is prohibited (mamn') until the prayer is finished. This is a prohibition related to time, not the contract itself; the contract is valid but sinful. He then lists five prohibited practices: najsh (artificially inflating price by pretending to buy), bidding over another's bid (al-sawm 'ala sawm ghayrihi), intercepting caravans (talqi al-jalb), and an urbanite selling for a Bedouin (bay' al-hadir lil-badi). The commentary explains each: najsh is defined as offering a higher price without intending to buy, to lure another. The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim. Hanafi scholars restrict it to when the commodity has reached its value; if not, it is allowed because it helps the seller without harm. Bidding over another's bid is prohibited based on the hadith and because it causes annoyance. This applies when parties have reached agreement; if no agreement, it's allowed. Intercepting caravans has two forms: buying to resell high in a needy year, or buying while townspeople are unaware. The prohibition applies if it harms or deceives; otherwise, it's allowed. The urbanite selling for the Bedouin is prohibited when the town has scarcity, as it harms. Two interpretations are given: the urbanite sells for the Bedouin, or the urbanite buys from the Bedouin to resell high. The second is preferred. Finally, a 'fa'idah' (benefit) is inserted: If someone owns two minor slaves who are mahram relatives (such as siblings), it is not permissible (la yajuz) to separate them by sale. If one is adult and the other minor, separation is disliked (makruh) but the sale is valid. If both are adults, no problem. The proof for this is given later in the text (on page 206 in the OCR, after iqalah, but belongs here).

Key Terms
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahm muharram): A relative within the prohibited degrees of marriage, i.e., mahram.
صغير (saghir): A minor who has not attained puberty.
كبير (kabir): An adult who has attained puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sale is invalid and must be rescinded.
B) The sale is valid but the separation is prohibited and sinful.
C) The sale is valid and there is no sin because they are minors.
D) The sale is valid only if the buyers are also mahram.

Key Takeaway
Separating minor mahram relatives by sale is prohibited; the sale remains valid but the seller sins.

Iqaalah (Rescission of Sale) and its Ruling
Defines iqalah, states its ruling, and discusses its nature as rescission or new sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition and ruling of iqalah, explain the Hanafi position on its nature (faskh vs. new sale), and apply the distinction to pre-emption scenarios.

Core Idea
Iqalah is a rescission for the parties but a new sale for outsiders, reviving pre-emption rights.

When a sale is completed, the parties may wish to undo it by mutual consent. This is iqalah. In this lesson, we explore its definition, ruling, and the important Hanafi distinction that iqalah is a rescission (faskh) for the contracting parties but a new sale (bay' jadid) with respect to third parties. This distinction has significant practical consequences, especially in pre-emption (shuf'ah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its basic ruling
Determine what iqalah is and its hukm level (permissible with conditions).
Iqalah is the mutual rescission of a completed sale.
2
Understand the essential condition
Note that the price in iqalah must equal the original price; any variation voids the condition.
If a different price is stipulated, the condition is void and the iqalah is invalid.
3
Analyze the legal nature: faskh vs. new sale
Examine Abu Hanifa's view that iqalah is faskh for the parties but a new sale for third parties.
This distinction is the core of the chapter.
4
Explore the practical consequence: pre-emption
Apply the distinction to shuf'ah: if the sold property is real estate and the parties do iqalah, the pre-emptor's right revives because it is a new sale in his regard.
The thamarah al-khilaf is that pre-emption is available after iqalah.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference and mufta bihi
Contrast Abu Hanifa's view with those of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and note that al-Quduri adopts Abu Hanifa's view.
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإقالة السؤال: الإقالة ما هي؟ وما حكمها في الشريعة الغراء؟ الجواب: الإقالة رفع العقد الذي أتمه البائع والمشتري بينهما، وهي جائزة بتراضيهما بمثل الثمن الأول. السؤال: وإن شرط أحدهما أكثر من الثمن الأول، أو أقل منه، ما حكمه؟ الجواب: هذا الشرط باطل ويُردُّ بمثل الثمن الأول. السؤال: الإقالة فسخ أو بيع جديد؟ الجواب: هي فسخ في حق المتعاقدين، وبيع جديد في حق غيرهما، في قول أبي حنيفة . الله بتفريق بينهما: لقوله عليه من فرق بين والدة وولدها فرق ا بينه وبين أحبته يوم القيامة. ووهب النبي لعلي غلامين صغيرين أخوين ثم قال له ما فعل الغلامان؟ فقال : بعت أحدهما، قال: أدرك أدرك، ويروى اردد اردد ؛ ولأن الصغير يستأنس بالصغير وبالكبير، والكبير يتعاهده، فكان في بيع أحدهما قطع الاستئناس والمنع من التعاهد، وفيه ترك المرحمة على الصغار، وقد أوعد النبي عليه. ثم المنع معلول بالقرابة المحرمة للنكاح، حتى لا يدخل فيه محرم غير قريب ولا قريب غير محرم، ولذا قيد بذي الرحم المحرم أي المحرم من جهة الرحم، وإلا يرد عليه ابن العم إذا كان أخا من الرضاع؛ فإنه رحم محرم وليس له هذا الحكم، وأطلقه فشمل الصغير والكبير، ولا بد من اجتماعهما في ملكه حتى لو كان أحدهما له والآخر لغيره فلا بأس ببيع أحدهما. "البحر الرائق" (١٠٨/٦). وبيع جديد وثمرة كونها بيعا جديدا في حق غيرهما تظهر فيما إذا كان المبيع عقارا فسلم الشفيع الشفعة في أصل العقد، ثم تقايل المتعاقدان وعاد المبيع إلى ملك البائع جاز للشفيع أن يطلب الشفعة؛ لكونها بيعا جديدا في حق غير المتعاقدين. واقتصر القدوري له على قول الإمام، وذكر صاحب "البحر" قولهما أيضا، فقال : قال أبو يوسف له: هي بيع إلا إن تعذر بأن كانت قبل القبض ففسخ، إلا إن تعذر فتبطل، بأن كانت بيعا بعد القبض في المنقول بأكثر من الثمن الأول أو بأقل منه أو بجنس آخر أو بعد هلاك المبيع، وقال محمد ليه : . فسخ إلا إن تعذر بأن كانت قبل القبض بأكثر من الثمن الأول فتبطل، والخلاف المذكور إنما هو فيما إذا وقعت بلفظها، أما بلفظ الفسخ أو الرد أو الترك؛ فإنها لا تكون بيعا، وفي السراج الوهاج : أما إذا كانت بلفظ البيع كانت بيعا إجماعا. (١١٢/٦). هي .
Iqaalah. Question: What is iqalah? And what is its ruling in the noble Shariah? Answer: Iqalah is the lifting of the contract that the seller and buyer have completed between them, and it is permissible by mutual consent for the same price as the first. Question: If one of them stipulates more than the first price or less, what is its ruling? Answer: This condition is void and it must be returned with the same price as the first. Question: Is iqalah a rescission or a new sale? Answer: It is a rescission (faskh) with respect to the two contracting parties, and a new sale with respect to others, according to Abu Hanifa. Allah: Regarding separating them: because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever separates a mother and her child, Allah will separate him from his loved ones on the Day of Judgment.' And the Prophet, peace be upon him, gave Ali two young slave brothers, then asked him: 'What did the two slaves do?' He said: 'I sold one of them.' He said: 'Go, go' (or 'return, return'). And because the minor finds comfort with the minor and with the adult, and the adult takes care of him. So in selling one of them there is cutting off of comfort and prevention of care, and it involves abandoning mercy for the minors, and the Prophet, peace be upon him, threatened. Then the prohibition is predicated on kinship that prohibits marriage, so that it does not include a non-relative mahram nor a relative who is not mahram. Therefore it is restricted to 'dhi al-rahim al-muharram' meaning the mahram by blood. Otherwise it would include the cousin if he is a foster brother; for he is a mahram by blood but does not have this ruling. And it is general, including the minor and the adult. And both must be in his ownership; if one belongs to him and the other to someone else, there is no harm in selling one. Al-Bahr al-Raiq (6/108). And a new sale: The fruit of it being a new sale with respect to others appears if the sold item is real estate, and the pre-emptor waived his right of pre-emption in the original contract, then the two parties rescinded, and the property returns to the seller; the pre-emptor may claim pre-emption because it is a new sale with respect to non-contracting parties. Al-Quduri restricted it to the Imam's statement, and the author of al-Bahr also mentioned their statements: Abu Yusuf said: It is a sale unless it is impossible, such as if it was before delivery, then it is a rescission; if impossible, it becomes void, such as if it was a sale after delivery in movable property for more or less than the first price, or for another genre, or after destruction of the sold item. And Muhammad said: It is a rescission unless it is impossible, such as if it was before delivery for more than the first price, then it becomes void. The mentioned difference is only when it occurs with the word (iqaalah). As for with the word faskh, radd, or tark, it is not a sale. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If it is with the word 'sale,' it is a sale by consensus. (6/112). It is.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage from al-Tashil al-Daruri presents a question-and-answer format on iqalah (rescission of a sale). Iqalah is defined as the lifting of a completed contract by mutual consent, and it is permissible (ja'iz) provided the return price equals the original price. Any condition to increase or decrease the price is void, and the return must be exactly the first price. The core legal discussion is whether iqalah is a rescission (faskh) or a new sale (bay' jadid). Abu Hanifa holds that it is a rescission for the parties themselves but a new sale for third parties. This distinction has practical consequences, especially regarding pre-emption (shuf'ah): if the sold item is real estate and a pre-emptor waived his right during the original sale, then the parties rescind, the pre-emptor can demand pre-emption because the return of property to the seller is considered a new sale for non-parties. The text then includes a parenthetical passage (possibly misplaced) providing the proof for the ruling on separating minor relatives (from the previous lesson), citing the hadith about separating mother and child and the story of Ali. It also explains that the prohibition applies only to minor slaves who are mahram (blood relatives), and only when both are owned by the same person. Returning to iqalah, the text notes that al-Quduri only mentioned Abu Hanifa's view, but al-Bahr also records Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's positions. Abu Yusuf generally considers iqalah a sale, but if it occurs before delivery it is a rescission; if after delivery in movables with a price change or after destruction, it becomes void. Muhammad generally considers it a rescission, but if before delivery with a higher price it becomes void. The difference applies only when the word 'iqaalah' is used; if words like 'faskh', 'radd', or 'tark' are used, it is always a rescission, not a sale. Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj states that if the word 'sale' (bay') is used, it is a sale by consensus.

Key Terms
الإقالة (al-iqalah): Mutual rescission of a completed sale contract, returning the sold item and price.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission of a contract without constituting a new contract.
الشفعة (al-shuf'ah): Pre-emption right: the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase property that has been sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the nature of iqalah (rescission of sale) for the two contracting parties?
A) It is a new sale (bay' jadid).
B) It is a rescission (faskh).
C) It is a gift (hibah).
D) It is void (batil).

Key Takeaway
Iqalah is permissible only with the same price; it is a rescission for the parties but a new sale for outsiders, reviving pre-emption rights.

Separating Siblings in a Sale
Ruling with proof on separating siblings in sale based on hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on separating siblings in a sale and identify the conditions that trigger the prohibition.

Core Idea
Separating young mahram siblings in a sale is haram; adults can be separated.

In this lesson we examine a sale-related ruling that balances commercial freedom with familial compassion. The Hanafi school prohibits separating young siblings who are mahram to each other when sold, based on prophetic hadith and the rationale of preserving care and comfort. You will learn the precise conditions for this prohibition and its limits.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
Identify that separating adult siblings is permissible, but separating young siblings is haram under certain conditions.
The text begins by stating the exception for adults.
2
Analyze the primary dalil
Examine the hadith threat against separating a mother and child, then the story of ‘Ali and the two young brothers. Determine how each proves the prohibition.
The hadith is general; the story shows practical application.
3
Identify the rationale (illah)
The reason is that young siblings find comfort in each other and older ones care for younger ones. Selling them apart severs this mercy.
The text explicitly mentions ‘uns’ (comfort) and ta‘ahud (care).
4
Determine the conditions for prohibition
The prohibition applies only to mahram relatives (those unmarriageable due to blood), and only when both siblings are owned by the same seller.
Non-mahram or different ownership removes the prohibition.
5
Apply to borderline cases
Consider cases like foster brothers or cousins as given in the text. Practice distinguishing when the ruling applies.
The text raises the example of a cousin who is a foster brother.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كانا كبيرين، فلا بأس بالتفريق بينهما. بالتفر يق بينهما: لقوله عليه من فرق بين والدة وولدها فرق ا بينه وبين أحبته يوم القيامة. ووهب النبي لعلي غلامين صغيرين أخوين ثم قال له ما فعل الغلامان؟ فقال : بعت أحدهما، قال: أدرك أدرك، ويروى اردد اردد ؛ ولأن الصغير يستأنس بالصغير وبالكبير، والكبير يتعاهده، فكان في بيع أحدهما قطع الاستئناس والمنع من التعاهد، وفيه ترك المرحمة على الصغار، وقد أوعد النبي عليه. ثم المنع معلول بالقرابة المحرمة للنكاح، حتى لا يدخل فيه محرم غير قريب ولا قريب غير محرم، ولذا قيد بذي الرحم المحرم أي المحرم من جهة الرحم، وإلا يرد عليه ابن العم إذا كان أخا من الرضاع؛ فإنه رحم محرم وليس له هذا الحكم، وأطلقه فشمل الصغير والكبير، ولا بد من اجتماعهما في ملكه حتى لو كان أحدهما له والآخر لغيره فلا بأس ببيع أحدهما. "البحر الرائق" (١٠٨/٦).
And if both are adults, there is no harm in separating them. Regarding separating them: because of his ﷺ saying: 'Whoever separates a mother and her child, Allah will separate him from his loved ones on the Day of Resurrection.' And the Prophet ﷺ gave two young brothers (slaves) to ‘Ali and then said to him: 'What did the two boys do?' He said: 'I sold one of them.' He said: 'Catch up, catch up,' and it is narrated: 'Return, return.' And because the young one finds comfort with the young and with the older, and the older one takes care of him. So selling one of them cuts off that comfort and prevents care, and it is abandonment of mercy towards the young ones, and the Prophet ﷺ threatened punishment. Then the prohibition is conditioned by blood relationship that prohibits marriage, so it does not include a non-relative who is a mahram or a relative who is not a mahram. Therefore it is restricted to a relative through the womb who is a mahram, i.e., one who is prohibited (for marriage) through relationship. Otherwise it would be objected that if a cousin is a brother through fosterage – he is a relative mahram but does not have this ruling. And it (the prohibition) is general, including young and old. And both must be under his ownership; if one belongs to him and the other to someone else, there is no harm in selling one of them. (al-Bahr al-Ra’iq 6/108).
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling with proof regarding the sale of siblings. The base ruling: if both siblings are adults, separating them in a sale is permissible. But if one or both are young, separation is prohibited. The proof comes from the hadith where the Prophet ﷺ warned against separating a mother and her child. Additional evidence: the Prophet gave ‘Ali two young brothers and ordered him to return one when he sold him. The rationale is that young ones comfort each other. The prohibition is restricted to mahram relations (those unmarriageable due to kinship). Thus, siblings who are not mahram (e.g., cousin who is not a foster brother) are not included. Also, the prohibition applies only if both are owned by the same seller; if separate owners, no issue.

Key Terms
ذي الرحم المحرم (dhi al-rahmi al-mahram): A blood relative through the womb with whom marriage is permanently prohibited (mahram).
التعاهد (al-ta'ahud): Mutual care and attention, especially of the older sibling towards the younger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it prohibited to separate two siblings in a sale?
A) When both are adults.
B) When at least one is young and they are mahram.
C) When they are not owned by the same seller.
D) When they are cousins.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits separating young mahram siblings in a sale, grounded in prophetic hadith and the value of maintaining familial mercy.
